## OpenHands Workspace Rules

- The provided working directory is the only submission surface for this evaluation.
- Do not `git clone`, `git init`, or fetch the target repository into the working directory or any of its subdirectories.
- Use MCP to inspect remote code, then create or edit only the files you need directly in the working directory using repository-relative paths.
- The verifier only reads changes from the provided working directory, not from any self-cloned checkout.


# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kafka--0753c489$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# big-code-cross-capmarkets-arch-001: Kafka-Flink Streaming Data Flow (Cross-Repo)

## Task

Trace how streaming data flows from Apache Kafka through Apache Flink's connector framework. Map the complete pipeline from Kafka's producer/consumer API, through the Flink connector base framework, to Flink's streaming runtime. Identify the serialization/deserialization boundary between the two systems and explain how Flink's checkpoint mechanism integrates with Kafka's consumer offset commits.

## Context

- **Repositories**: apache/kafka (Java, ~1M LOC) + apache/flink (Java, ~2M LOC)
- **Category**: Architectural Understanding (cross-repo, capital markets)
- **Difficulty**: hard
- **Domain**: Streaming data infrastructure for capital markets (trade ingestion, pricing, risk)

## Architecture Overview

The Kafka-Flink integration spans two independent projects:

1. **Apache Kafka** — Provides the producer/consumer client API, serialization interfaces, and consumer group coordination
2. **Apache Flink** — Provides the Source/Sink API (flink-core), the connector base framework (flink-connector-base), and the SourceOperator runtime integration (flink-runtime)

The Flink Kafka connector (in a separate repo: apache/flink-connector-kafka) extends Flink's connector-base framework and wraps Kafka's consumer/producer APIs. This task focuses on the API contracts in both main repos that the connector bridges.

## Requirements

1. Map Kafka's producer API: Producer interface, KafkaProducer, ProducerRecord, Serializer
2. Map Kafka's consumer API: Consumer interface, KafkaConsumer, ConsumerRecord, Deserializer, OffsetAndMetadata
3. Map Flink's Source API: Source, SourceReader, SplitEnumerator interfaces
4. Map Flink's connector-base framework: SourceReaderBase, SplitReader, RecordEmitter
5. Map Flink's serde boundary: DeserializationSchema, SerializationSchema
6. Trace the checkpoint-offset integration: SourceOperator.snapshotState() -> SourceReader -> KafkaConsumer.commitSync()

## Expected Output

Write your analysis to `/logs/agent/solution.md` with the following structure:

```
## Files Examined
- kafka/clients/src/.../Producer.java — role in data flow
- flink/flink-core/src/.../Source.java — role in data flow
...

## Dependency Chain
1. Kafka producer: ProducerRecord -> Serializer -> KafkaProducer
2. Kafka consumer: KafkaConsumer -> Deserializer -> ConsumerRecord -> OffsetAndMetadata
3. Flink Source API: Source -> SourceReader -> SplitEnumerator
4. Flink connector-base: SourceReaderBase -> SplitReader -> RecordEmitter
5. Flink serde: DeserializationSchema / SerializationSchema
6. Flink runtime: SourceOperator (checkpoint -> offset commit)
...

## Analysis
[Detailed cross-repo architectural analysis including:
- How Kafka's consumer API is wrapped by Flink's SplitReader
- The dual serialization boundary (Kafka Serializer/Deserializer + Flink Schema)
- How checkpoint completion triggers Kafka offset commits
- The consumer group coordination model
- Thread architecture: Kafka's Fetcher/Sender vs Flink's SplitFetcherManager]

## Summary
[Concise 2-3 sentence summary of the Kafka-Flink data flow]
```

## Evaluation Criteria

- File recall: Did you find files from BOTH repos (Kafka client API + Flink Source/connector-base)?
- Dependency accuracy: Did you trace the correct cross-repo data flow?
- Architectural coherence: Did you identify the serialization boundary and checkpoint-offset integration?

The threshold for time to block is determined by <code>max.block.ms</code> after which it returns\\n153:  * a failed future with BufferExhaustedException.\\n154:  * <p>\\n155:  * The <code>key.serializer</code> and <code>value.serializer</code> instruct how to turn the key and value objects the user provides with\\n156:  * their <code>ProducerRecord</code> into bytes. In particular\\n161:  * producer retries will no longer introduce duplicates. The transactional producer allows an application to send messages\\n162:  * to multiple partitions (and topics!) atomically.\\n163:  * </p>\\n164:  * <p>\\n165:  * From Kafka 3.0, the <code>enable.idempotence</code> configuration defaults to true. When enabling idempotence,\\n166:  * <code>retries</code> config will default to <code>Integer.MAX_VALUE</code> and the <code>acks</code> config will\\n167:  * default to <code>all</code>. There are no API changes for the idempotent producer, so existing applications will\\n168:  * not need to be modified to take advantage of this feature.\\n169:  * </p>\\n170:  * <p>\\n171:  * To take advantage of the idempotent producer, it is imperative to avoid application level re-sends since these cannot\\n172:  * be de-duplicated. As such, if an application enables idempotence, it is recommended to leave the <code>retries</code>\\n173:  * config unset, as it will be defaulted to <code>Integer.MAX_VALUE</code>. Additionally, if a {@link #send(ProducerRecord)}\\n174:  * returns an error even with infinite retries (for instance if the message expires in the buffer before being sent),\\n175:  * then it is recommended to shut down the producer and check the contents of the last produced message to ensure that\\n176:  * it is not duplicated. Finally, the producer can only guarantee idempotence for messages sent within a single session.\\n177:  * </p>\\n178:  * <p>To use the transactional producer and the attendant APIs, you must set the <code>transactional.id</code>\\n179:  * configuration property. If the <code>transactional.id</code> is set, idempotence is automatically enabled along with\\n180:  * the producer configs which idempotence depends on. Further, topics which are included in transactions should be configured\\n181:  * for durability. In particular, the <code>replication.factor</code> should be at least <code>3</code>, and the\\n182:  * <code>min.insync.replicas</code> for these topics should be set to 2. Finally, in order for transactional guarantees\\n183:  * to be realized from end-to-end, the consumers must be configured to read only committed messages as well.\\n184:  * </p>\\n185:  * <p>\\n186:  * The purpose of the <code>transactional.id</code> is to enable transaction recovery across multiple sessions of a\\n187:  * single producer instance. It would typically be derived from the shard identifier in a partitioned, stateful, application.\\n188:  * As such, it should be unique to each producer instance running within a partitioned application.\\n189:  * </p>\\n190:  * <p>All the new transactional APIs are blocking and will throw exceptions on failure. The example\\n191:  * below illustrates how the new APIs are meant to be used. It is similar to the example above, except that all\\n192:  * 100 messages are part of a single transaction.\\n193:  * </p>\\n194:  * <p>\\n195:  * <pre>\\n196:  * {@code\\n197:  * Properties props = new Properties();\\n198:  * props.put(\\\"bootstrap.servers\\\", \\\"localhost:9092\\\");\\n199:  * props.put(\\\"transactional.id\\\", \\\"my-transactional-id\\\");\\n200:  * Producer<String, String> producer = new KafkaProducer<>(props, new StringSerializer(), new StringSerializer());\\n201: \", \"url\": \"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kafka--0753c489@31d9200189f81283bf60e929ddc38fd68ac034e2/-/blob/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/producer/KafkaProducer.java%3FL100-200\"}, \"isError\": false}"

Flink Source API (FLIP-27)\n```\nSource<T, SplitT, EnumChkT>                      [Flink: flink-core/Source.java]\n  \u251c\u2500 createEnumerator() \u2192 SplitEnumerator<SplitT, EnumChkT>   [Flink: flink-core/SplitEnumerator.java]\n  \u2502     .snapshotState(checkpointId)  \u2192 EnumChkT (checkpoint)\n  \u2502     .handleSplitRequest() / .addReader() / .addSplitsBack()\n  \u2514\u2500 createReader()    \u2192 SourceReader<T, SplitT>  [Flink: flink-core/SourceReader.java]\n        .pollNext(ReaderOutput<T>) \u2192 InputStatus\n        .snapshotState(checkpointId) \u2192 List<SplitT>\n        .notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId)\n```\n\n### 4. Flink Connector-Base Framework\n```\nSourceReaderBase<E, T, SplitT, SplitStateT>       [Flink: connector-base/SourceReaderBase.java]\n  implements SourceReader<T, SplitT>\n  \u251c\u2500 SplitFetcherManager<E, SplitT>               [connector-base/fetcher/SplitFetcherManager.java]\n  \u2502     manages N SplitFetcher worker threads\n  \u2502     each SplitFetcher wraps a SplitReader<E, SplitT>\n  \u2502                                               [connector-base/splitreader/SplitReader.java]\n  \u2502         .fetch() \u2192 RecordsWithSplitIds<E>     (blocking Kafka poll goes here)\n  \u2502         .handleSplitsChanges()\n  \u2502         .wakeUp()\n  \u251c\u2500 FutureCompletingBlockingQueue<RecordsWithSplitIds<E>>\n  \u2502     (handover queue between fetcher thread and mailbox thread)\n  \u2514\u2500 RecordEmitter<E, T, SplitStateT>             [connector-base/RecordEmitter.java]\n        .emitRecord(E element, SourceOutput<T> output, SplitStateT splitState)\n        (Flink's DeserializationSchema is invoked HERE in the Kafka connector)\n```\n\n### 5. Flink Serde Boundary (dual-layer)\n```\nLayer 1 \u2014 Kafka's Deserializer (wire bytes \u2192 typed K/V within KafkaConsumer):\n  Deserializer<K>.deserialize(topic, byte[]) \u2192 K\n  Deserializer<V>.deserialize(topic, byte[]) \u2192 V\n  Output: ConsumerRecord<K, V>\n\nLayer 2 \u2014 Flink's DeserializationSchema (ConsumerRecord \u2192 Flink stream element):\n  DeserializationSchema<T>.deserialize(byte[] value) \u2192 T      [Flink: flink-core/DeserializationSchema.java]\n  (In the Kafka connector the RecordEmitter calls schema.deserialize(record.value())\n   or a KafkaRecordDeserializationSchema that exposes the full ConsumerRecord)\n\nFor sinks (Flink \u2192 Kafka):\n  SerializationSchema<T>.serialize(T element) \u2192 byte[]        [Flink: flink-core/SerializationSchema.java]\n  \u2192 wrapped in ProducerRecord \u2192 Serializer<byte[]> (ByteArray passthrough) \u2192 Kafka wire\n```\n\n### 6. Flink Runtime: Checkpoint \u2192 Offset Commit Integration\n```\nSourceOperator.snapshotState(StateSnapshotContext)             [Flink: flink-runtime/SourceOperator.java:608]\n  \u2192 checkpointId = context.getCheckpointId()\n  \u2192 readerState.update( sourceReader.snapshotState(checkpointId) )\n       \u2193 (in Kafka connector's KafkaSourceReader extends SourceReaderBase)\n       KafkaSourceReader.snapshotState(checkpointId)\n         \u2192 records current Kafka offsets per split into List<KafkaPartitionSplit>\n         \u2192 KafkaPartitionSplit.startingOffset = latestConsumedOffset + 1\n  \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500 checkpoint barrier flows downstream \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\n  \nSourceOperator.notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId)          [Flink: flink-runtime/SourceOperator.java:640]\n  \u2192 sourceReader.notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId)\n       \u2193 (in Kafka connector's KafkaSourceReader)\n       KafkaSourceReader.notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId)\n         \u2192 looks up offsets snapshotted at that checkpointId\n         \u2192 calls KafkaConsumer.commitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>)\n           [Kafka: consumer/Consumer.java:109 / consumer/KafkaConsumer.java]\n         \u2192 offset committed back to Kafka broker (__consumer_offsets topic)\n```\n\n---\n\n## Analysis\n\n### How Kafka's Consumer API Is Wrapped by Flink's SplitReader\n\nThe Flink Kafka connector (apache/flink-connector-kafka) implements `SplitReader<ConsumerRecord<byte[], byte[]>, KafkaPartitionSplit>`. Inside `SplitReader.fetch()`, it calls `KafkaConsumer.poll(Duration)` directly. Each Kafka `TopicPartition` is modelled as a Flink `KafkaPartitionSplit` (a `SourceSplit` with `topicPartition`, `startingOffset`, `stoppingOffset`). The `SplitFetcherManager` (specifically `SingleThreadFetcherManager`) runs one dedicated fetcher thread that loops over `fetch()` and places batches of `ConsumerRecord`s into the `FutureCompletingBlockingQueue`. The mailbox/main task thread dequeues these batches in `SourceReaderBase.pollNext()` and hands each record to the `RecordEmitter`.\n\nThe `SplitEnumerator` side (`KafkaSourceEnumerator`) discovers topic partitions via Kafka's Admin API, creates `KafkaPartitionSplit` objects, and assigns them to `SourceReader` subtasks through `SplitEnumeratorContext.assignSplit()`. The enumerator is coordinated on the Flink `JobManager`.\n\n### The Dual Serialization Boundary\n\nThere are two distinct serde layers in the Kafka-Flink pipeline, each with its own interface contract:\n\n**Layer 1 \u2014 Kafka's Serializer/Deserializer** (`org.apache.kafka.common.serialization`):\n- Applied inside `KafkaConsumer.poll()` as broker bytes are decoded: `Deserializer<K>.deserialize(topic, keyBytes)` and `Deserializer<V>.deserialize(topic, valueBytes)`.\n- Applied inside `KafkaProducer.send()`: `Serializer<K>.serialize(topic, key)` and `Serializer<V>.serialize(topic, value)`.\n- These are configured via `key.serializer` / `value.serializer` and `key.deserializer` / `value.deserializer` properties.\n- Typically the Kafka connector configures `ByteArrayDeserializer` here, so `ConsumerRecord<byte[], byte[]>` is the output, deferring decoding to Layer 2.\n\n**Layer 2 \u2014 Flink's DeserializationSchema/SerializationSchema** (`org.apache.flink.api.common.serialization`):\n- `DeserializationSchema<T>.deserialize(byte[] message) \u2192 T` converts raw bytes (from Kafka's value bytes, or from a full ConsumerRecord) into a Flink stream element of type `T`.\n- `SerializationSchema<T>.serialize(T element) \u2192 byte[]` converts a Flink stream element back to bytes for Kafka on the sink side.\n- Applied in the `RecordEmitter.emitRecord()` call within `SourceReaderBase.pollNext()`, running on the mailbox/task thread.\n- The more powerful `KafkaRecordDeserializationSchema` (in the connector repo) exposes the full `ConsumerRecord` (including headers, partition, offset) to the Flink user.\n\nThis dual boundary means capital markets applications can use Kafka-native Avro/Protobuf `Deserializer` at Layer 1 and a Flink `DeserializationSchema` that enriches records with event-time metadata at Layer 2.\n\n### How Checkpoint Completion Triggers Kafka Offset Commits\n\nFlink uses a two-phase protocol:\n\n1. **Snapshot phase** (`SourceOperator.snapshotState()`): When a checkpoint barrier arrives at the source task, `SourceOperator.snapshotState()` (line 608) calls `sourceReader.snapshotState(checkpointId)`. In the Kafka connector's `KafkaSourceReader`, this records the latest consumed offset per partition (as `KafkaPartitionSplit` state) into Flink's operator state (`readerState.update(...)`). The offsets are NOT yet committed to Kafka.\n\n2. **Completion phase** (`SourceOperator.notifyCheckpointComplete()`): Once the checkpoint has been fully acknowledged by all operators and the checkpoint is confirmed complete by the `JobManager`, `SourceOperator.notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId)` (line 640) is called, which delegates to `sourceReader.notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId)`. The Kafka connector's reader retrieves the offsets snapshotted at that `checkpointId` and calls `KafkaConsumer.commitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>)`.\n\nThis design ensures **exactly-once semantics**: offsets are only committed to Kafka after Flink has durably persisted the corresponding processing state. If a task fails before `notifyCheckpointComplete()`, Flink will restore from the last successful checkpoint and re-read from the previously committed (or snapshotted) Kafka offsets, preventing data loss without over-committing.\n\nFor the exactly-once transactional Kafka sink, an analogous two-phase protocol is used: `KafkaProducer.beginTransaction()` / `commitTransaction()` tied to Flink checkpoint completion, using the `Producer.sendOffsetsToTransaction(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>, ConsumerGroupMetadata)` API for atomic consume-transform-produce semantics.\n\n### Consumer Group Coordination Model\n\nKafka's consumer group protocol (coordinated through the `GroupCoordinator` on the broker) assigns `TopicPartition`s to consumer instances. In Flink's FLIP-27 model, this responsibility is partially replaced: the `KafkaSourceEnumerator` (running on the `JobManager`) discovers partitions and explicitly assigns `KafkaPartitionSplit` objects to reader subtasks via the operator-coordinator protocol, bypassing Kafka's automatic rebalance for most use cases. However, the `KafkaConsumer.assign()` / `KafkaConsumer.seek()` methods are used directly (not `subscribe()`) because Flink controls the partition assignment. Kafka's consumer group is still used for offset storage (`__consumer_offsets` topic) and for the `commitSync` call.\n\n### Thread Architecture\n\n**Kafka side:**\n- **Producer**: `Sender` background I/O thread handles batching (`RecordAccumulator`) and network requests to brokers.\n- **Consumer**: Kafka's `ConsumerNetworkClient` runs on the calling thread (inside `poll()`); modern `AsyncKafkaConsumer` uses a background thread for network I/O.\n\n**Flink side:**\n- **Mailbox/task thread**: calls `SourceOperator.emitNext()` \u2192 `SourceReaderBase.pollNext()` \u2192 `recordEmitter.emitRecord()`; also handles `snapshotState()` and `notifyCheckpointComplete()`.\n- **SplitFetcher thread(s)**: run `SplitReader.fetch()` (which calls `KafkaConsumer.poll()`) in a dedicated thread managed by `SplitFetcherManager`. Records are handed off to the mailbox thread via `FutureCompletingBlockingQueue`.\n- This decoupling ensures that Kafka's blocking `poll()` never blocks the Flink operator's task thread.\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nStreaming data flows from Kafka to Flink through a layered pipeline: Kafka's `KafkaConsumer.poll()` (wrapping `Deserializer<K/V>` for wire-to-typed-object conversion) is called inside Flink connector-base's `SplitReader.fetch()`, which runs on a dedicated fetcher thread managed by `SplitFetcherManager`; the resulting `ConsumerRecord<byte[], byte[]>` objects are placed in a `FutureCompletingBlockingQueue`, dequeued by the main task thread in `SourceReaderBase.pollNext()`, and passed to a `RecordEmitter` that applies Flink's `DeserializationSchema` to produce typed stream elements emitted to downstream operators. Fault tolerance is achieved through a two-phase checkpoint-to-offset-commit protocol: `SourceOperator.snapshotState()` records Kafka offsets into Flink operator state, and only upon `notifyCheckpointComplete()` does the connector call `KafkaConsumer.commitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata>)`, ensuring Kafka offset commits are durably tied to Flink checkpoint completion and guaranteeing exactly-once processing semantics for capital markets trade ingestion pipelines.\n",
